###begin article-title 0
###xml 4 19 4 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila Pax6</italic>
The Drosophila Pax6 paralogs have different functions in head development but can partially substitute for each other
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Communicated by T. Clandinin.
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 14 18 14 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 28 51 28 51 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila melanogaster</italic>
###xml 53 60 53 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eyeless</italic>
###xml 62 64 62 64 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 70 85 70 85 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">twin-of-eyeless</italic>
###xml 87 90 87 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 255 258 255 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 262 264 262 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 330 332 330 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 447 449 447 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 449 450 449 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;</italic>
###xml 449 450 449 450 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>&#8722;</italic></sup>
###xml 508 512 508 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 622 630 622 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy-Gal4</italic>
###xml 665 669 665 669 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 681 684 681 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 756 759 756 759 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 858 861 858 861 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 981 984 981 984 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1068 1070 1068 1070 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1245 1249 1245 1249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 28 51 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila melanogaster</span>
There are two Pax6 genes in Drosophila melanogaster; eyeless (ey) and twin-of-eyeless (toy), due to a duplication, which most likely occurred in the insect lineage. They encode transcription factors important for head development. Misexpression of either toy or ey can induce formation of ectopic compound eyes. Toy regulates the ey gene by binding to an eye-specific enhancer in its second intron. However, Toy can induce ectopic eyes also in an ey- background, which indicates a redundancy between the two Pax6 copies in eye formation. To elucidate to what extent these two genes are interchangeable, we first generated toy-Gal4 constructs capable of driving the Pax6 genes in a toy-specific manner. Genetic dissection of the promoter proximal region of toy identified a 1,300-bp region around the canonical transcription start that is sufficient to drive toy expression in embryonic brain and eye primorida and in larval eye-antennal discs. We find that exogenous expression of toy can partially rescue the lethality and eye phenotype caused by lethal mutations in ey and vice versa. We therefore conclude that Toy and Ey, to some extent, can substitute for each other. Nevertheless, the phenotypes of the rescued flies indicate that the two Pax6 genes are specialized to regulate defined structures of the fly head.
###end p 2

###end title 3

###end p 4
###begin title 5
Keywords
###end title 5
###begin title 6
Introduction
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 4 14 4 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 315 325 315 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ocelliless</italic>
###xml 327 337 327 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">buttonhead</italic>
###xml 339 354 339 354 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">empty spiracles</italic>
###xml 359 367 359 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">tailless</italic>
###xml 465 469 465 469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR16">1991</xref>
###xml 671 675 671 675 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR8">2006</xref>
###xml 873 877 873 877 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR17">1969</xref>
The Drosophila body plan is established in the early embryo by gradients of maternally deposited mRNA and proteins. A positional coordinate system is formed by combinatorial genetic interactions between gene activators and repressors, subdividing the embryo into discrete domains. Specific cephalic gap genes, like ocelliless, buttonhead, empty spiracles and tailless, define the developmental pattern in the pregnathal region of the head (Finkelstein and Perrimon 1991). The different organs and appendages are then determined by downstream selector genes. At the cellular blastoderm stage, 6-23 cells are allocated to form the eye-antennal primordium (Callaerts et al. 2006). At the beginning of larval development there are about 20 cells, derived from multiple embryonic segments that proliferate to form a larval eye-antennal imaginal disc (Garcia-Bellido and Merriam 1969). After differentiation, this pair of discs will form most of the head capsule of the adult fly.
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax</italic>
###xml 177 181 177 181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR10">2002</xref>
###xml 319 322 319 322 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax</italic>
###xml 447 451 447 451 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR7">2000</xref>
###xml 467 471 467 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR36">2000</xref>
###xml 572 582 572 582 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 592 596 592 596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 604 619 604 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">twin-of-eyeless</italic>
###xml 621 624 621 624 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 630 637 630 637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eyeless</italic>
###xml 639 641 639 641 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 656 660 656 660 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 673 681 673 681 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eye gone</italic>
###xml 683 686 683 686 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eyg</italic>
###xml 692 708 692 708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">twin of eye gone</italic>
###xml 710 713 710 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toe</italic>
###xml 810 814 810 814 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">1995</xref>
###xml 830 834 830 834 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 848 852 848 852 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR25">2003</xref>
Pax genes play important roles in the development of the central nervous system (CNS) and brain, as well as of the peripheral nervous system and sensory organs (Chi and Epstein 2002). They encode transcription factors characterized by a 128-amino acid paired domain, which has a sequence-specific DNA-binding function. Pax genes have been divided into five subgroups based on sequence similarity between their paired domains (Breitling and Gerber 2000; Miller et al. 2000). Several Pax proteins, including Pax6, possess an additional DNA-binding domain, a homeodomain. In Drosophila, the two Pax6 genes: twin-of-eyeless (toy) and eyeless (ey), and the two Pax6-like genes: eye gone (eyg) and twin of eye gone (toe) are all expressed in the same developmental pathway controlling eye development (Halder et al. 1995; Czerny et al. 1999; Jang et al. 2003). How these proteins cooperate to specify the visual system is still under investigation.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 39 42 39 42 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 211 215 211 215 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 236 240 236 240 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR30">2001</xref>
###xml 364 367 364 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 543 547 543 547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR30">2001</xref>
###xml 561 564 561 564 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 638 640 638 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 707 709 707 709 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 717 720 717 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 725 727 725 727 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 795 805 795 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 915 919 915 919 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR30">2001</xref>
In situ hybridizations have shown that toy transcription is initiated at cellular blastoderm in the procephalic neuroectoderm, which gives rise to the primordia of the visual system and the brain (Czerny et al. 1999; Kammermeier et al. 2001). During gastrulation the expression is confined to the region anterior to the cephalic furrow and at germ band retraction toy mRNA is detected in the eye and brain primordia and in a reiterated segmental pattern in the ventral nerve cord (VNC), partially overlapping Ey expression (Kammermeier et al. 2001). In larvae, toy is expressed in certain parts of the brain and VNC, not overlapping with ey: however, in undifferentiated eye discs the pattern is similar to ey. Thus, toy and ey have overlapping expression in the developing visual system during Drosophila embryonic development and in the eye-antennal imaginal discs, but non-overlapping in CNS (Kammermeier et al. 2001).
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 54 56 54 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 133 135 133 135 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 156 160 156 160 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 213 215 213 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 298 302 298 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR21">1999</xref>
###xml 335 337 335 337 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 421 423 421 423 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 458 461 458 461 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 502 504 502 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 504 505 504 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 504 505 504 505 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 510 512 510 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 512 513 512 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 512 513 512 513 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>R</italic></sup>
###xml 537 541 537 541 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 561 565 561 565 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR44">2004</xref>
###xml 623 625 623 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 705 716 705 716 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">sine oculis</italic>
###xml 718 720 718 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">so</italic>
###xml 784 790 784 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atonal</italic>
###xml 861 865 861 865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR51">2006</xref>
###xml 890 893 890 893 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 942 946 942 946 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 973 975 973 975 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 975 976 975 976 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 975 976 975 976 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 980 982 980 982 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 982 983 982 983 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 982 983 982 983 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>R</italic></sup>
###xml 1038 1040 1038 1040 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1060 1062 1060 1062 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1062 1067 1062 1067 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 1062 1067 1062 1067 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 1082 1086 1082 1086 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR44">2004</xref>
###xml 1126 1128 1126 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1137 1139 1137 1139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1139 1140 1139 1140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1139 1140 1139 1140 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 1236 1239 1236 1239 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1239 1242 1239 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 1239 1242 1239 1242 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 1260 1264 1260 1264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 1284 1286 1284 1286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1286 1287 1286 1287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;</italic>
###xml 1286 1287 1286 1287 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>&#8722;</italic></sup>
###xml 1295 1302 1295 1302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Df(4)BA</italic>
###xml 1338 1340 1338 1340 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1340 1341 1340 1341 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1340 1341 1340 1341 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 1680 1682 1680 1682 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1682 1683 1682 1683 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1682 1683 1682 1683 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 1794 1798 1794 1798 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 1812 1814 1812 1814 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1819 1822 1819 1822 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1886 1890 1886 1890 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">1995</xref>
###xml 1906 1910 1906 1910 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 2001 2005 2001 2005 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
Biochemical data indicate that Toy directly regulates ey by binding to the eye-specific enhancer located in the second intron of the ey gene (Czerny et al. 1999). Mutations in Toy-binding sites within the minimal ey enhancer abolish reporter gene expression in the eye disc primordia (Hauck et al. 1999), but do not entirely eliminate ey expression in the posterior region of the eye discs or in the CNS, indicating that ey is also activated by other means. toy mRNA is present in the eye primordia of ey2 and eyR embryos (Czerny et al. 1999) and Punzo et al. (2004) showed that Toy can activate eye development also in an ey-independent manner, probably through its direct binding to the eye enhancer of sine oculis (so). Further on, Ey and So bind to cis-regulatory elements in the atonal gene, and thus directly control neurogenesis in the eye (Zhang et al. 2006). While null alleles of toy result in a headless phenotype (Kronhamn et al. 2002), the hypomorphic alleles ey2 or eyR only affect the compound eye development, as does the ey stated null mutant eyJ5.71 (Punzo et al. 2004). We have previously described another ey allele, eyD, which exhibits a dominant small-eyed phenotype and a recessive headless phenotype, similar to toyhdl (Kronhamn et al. 2002). Since hemizygous ey- flies (Df(4)BA/+) have a wild-type eye phenotype, eyD cannot be considered to be a null mutant. It is caused by an insertion of material from chromosome 2 in the 3' region of the gene, resulting in a truncated Ey protein which lacks the homeodomain. This protein probably has a dominant negative function, interfering with the wild-type Ey protein. There is extensive cell death occurring in eyD eye discs, and the phenotype can be rescued by targeted expression of an apoptosis inhibitor (Kronhamn et al. 2002). Since both ey and toy can give rise to ectopic eyes when misexpressed (Halder et al. 1995; Czerny et al. 1999) and since mutants in both genes can produce similar headless phenotypes (Kronhamn et al. 2002), we decided to investigate to what extent these two genes can substitute for each other.
###end p 10
###begin p 11
###xml 31 39 31 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy-Gal4</italic>
###xml 86 89 86 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 181 184 181 184 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 239 242 239 242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 650 653 650 653 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
We started out by constructing toy-Gal4 driver lines to be able to express genes in a toy-specific pattern. This was done by dissecting the 5' upstream cis-regulatory region of the toy gene. We identified a 1,300-bp region surrounding the toy transcription start which was sufficient to drive reporter genes with the expected expression pattern in embryonic eye-antennal primordia and brain as well as in larval eye-antennal discs. The same region was also found to generate headless pharate adults, when driving the expression of an RNAi transgene, which interferes with the translational machinery. This phenotype is similar to the one produced by toy null mutants.
###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 51 54 51 54 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 59 61 59 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 188 192 188 192 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR6">1994</xref>
###xml 271 274 271 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 344 346 344 346 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 367 371 367 371 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR4">1997</xref>
###xml 386 390 386 390 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR21">1999</xref>
###xml 405 409 405 409 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 544 547 544 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 552 554 552 554 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 628 631 628 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 631 634 631 634 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 631 634 631 634 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 639 642 639 642 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 642 647 642 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G7.39</italic>
###xml 642 647 642 647 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
###xml 830 833 830 833 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 833 836 833 836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 833 836 833 836 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
To eventually test possible redundancy between the toy and ey genes we set out to rescue the phenotypes of some lethal alleles in both genes, using the GAL4/UAS system (Brand and Perrimon 1994). To this end we used transgenic lines expressing Gal4 directed by either the toy 5' regulatory region generated or the eye-specific enhancer from the ey gene (Bonini et al. 1997; Hauck et al. 1999) to drive UAS-Pax6 genes and analyzed the viability and head phenotype of the rescued flies. We found that exogenous Toy could significantly rescue both toy and ey homozygous mutants to viability. Correspondingly, the pupal lethality of toyhdl and toyG7.39 mutants was rescued by expression of Ey. Partial rescue of the gene-specific eye phenotypes was also evident. Furthermore, we show that inhibition of apoptosis increased survival of toyhdl homozygotes, but did not improve eye phenotypes.
###end p 12
###begin title 13
Materials and methods
###end title 13
###begin title 14
GAL4 constructs
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 40 43 40 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 89 92 89 92 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 184 187 184 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 311 315 311 315 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 320 324 320 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy5</italic>
###xml 359 363 359 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3</italic>
###xml 434 438 434 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy4</italic>
###xml 472 476 472 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy6</italic>
###xml 511 515 511 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 517 521 517 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 523 527 523 527 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3</italic>
###xml 529 533 529 533 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy4</italic>
###xml 566 570 566 570 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy5</italic>
###xml 572 576 572 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy6</italic>
###xml 633 634 633 634 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig3" ref-type="fig">3</xref>
In order to study the regulation of the toy gene and to construct Gal4 driver lines with toy 5' cis-regulatory regions, six different genomic fragments from the region upstream of the toy transcription start were PCR amplified. We used the following primers: AGCTGGGATCCTATGGGATATGTATATATG (used for constructs toy1 and toy5); AGGCAAGGCATTTTGAACTCCTGGTACCGT (toy2); AATGGTACCGGGCAATAAATAACTAGTC (toy3); GAATCCATAATGTTAAAGGTACCCACGAT (toy4); TATGCACTAAGCAAATGGTACCGAAAGAG (toy6); TTAGGATCCTAATTAATTATTTTTAATGCG (toy1, toy2, toy3, toy4); ACGGATCCAGGAAGGTCAAACAGTATCA (toy5, toy6). (For extension and overlap between fragments see Fig. 3.)
###end p 15
###begin p 16
###xml 14 18 14 18 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 20 24 20 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3</italic>
###xml 26 31 26 31 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy4,</italic>
###xml 36 40 36 40 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy6</italic>
###xml 68 73 68 73 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pGaTB</italic>
###xml 123 127 123 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Gal4</italic>
###xml 140 143 140 143 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Not</italic>
###xml 149 152 149 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Kpn</italic>
###xml 174 186 174 186 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pP{CaSpeR-4}</italic>
###xml 213 217 213 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 222 227 222 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy5,</italic>
###xml 232 245 232 245 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Gal4::Hsp70Bb</italic>
###xml 257 262 257 262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pGaTB</italic>
###xml 287 290 287 290 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Kpn</italic>
###xml 296 299 296 299 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Sst</italic>
###xml 348 360 348 360 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pP{CaSpeR-4}</italic>
###xml 383 386 383 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Bam</italic>
###xml 410 414 410 414 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Gal4</italic>
###xml 434 437 434 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Bam</italic>
###xml 492 495 492 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Not</italic>
###xml 501 504 501 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Stu</italic>
###xml 583 587 583 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 592 596 592 596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy5</italic>
###xml 634 637 634 637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Bam</italic>
###xml 740 741 740 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">w</italic>
###xml 741 745 741 745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1118</italic>
###xml 741 745 741 745 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>1118</italic></sup>
The fragments toy2, toy3, toy4, and toy6 were first cloned into the pGaTB vector. They were then cut out together with the Gal4 gene, using NotI and KpnI, and ligated into a pP{CaSpeR-4} vector. For subcloning of toy1 and toy5, the Gal4::Hsp70Bb portion of pGaTB was first cut out using KpnI and SstII and then ligated into the polycloning site of pP{CaSpeR-4}. To generate a unique BamHI site upstream of the Gal4 coding region, the BamHI in the polycloning site was removed by cutting with NotI and StuI, treating with nuclease S1 to generate blunt ends and re-ligating. Fragments toy1 and toy5 were then ligated into the remaining BamHI site and clones were sequenced to confirm correct orientation. The constructs were transformed into w1118 embryos. Several independent inserts were generated for each construct. The number of analyzed lines is shown in Supplementary Table S1.
###end p 16
###begin title 17
Toy antibody production, Western blot and immunostaining
###end title 17
###begin p 18
###xml 429 432 429 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">y w</italic>
###xml 434 437 434 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 437 440 437 440 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 437 440 437 440 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 475 490 475 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hs-Gal4&gt;UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 1067 1071 1061 1065 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR39">1994</xref>
###xml 56 62 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 826 832 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 1134 1138 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goat</span>
###xml 1144 1150 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 1213 1218 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1284 1289 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1373 1379 <span type="species:ncbi:9793">Donkey</span>
###xml 1385 1390 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1575 1581 <span type="species:ncbi:9793">donkey</span>
###xml 1587 1593 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Polyclonal antiserum directed against Toy was raised in rabbit (Agrisera, Vannas, Sweden). Two Toy peptides that differ significantly from Ey, were simultaneously used as antigens: amino acids 209-224 and 531-543. The antiserum was affinity purified using an UltraLink matrix (Pierce) with neutral elution conditions using ActiSep Elution Reagent (Sterogene, USA). The affinity-purified serum was pre-absorbed against homozygous y w; toyhdl third instar larvae. Adult flies (hs-Gal4>UAS-toy and control) were heat-shocked at 37degrees for 45 min, left at room temperature for 30 min, heat-shocked again for 30 min and protein was prepared after another 45 min at room temperature. Western blots were done according to standard procedures, using the Toy antiserum as primary antibody (dilution 1:1,000) and HRP-conjugated anti-rabbit antibody (NA934, Amersham) (dilution 1:10,000) as secondary antibody. The immunoreactions were visualized with the ECL+ system (RPN2132, Amersham). Immunohistochemical analyses in embryos were carried out as per the methods of Patel (1994). The Toy antiserum was diluted 1:400 and a biotin-conjugated goat anti-rabbit antibody was used as secondary antibody (dilution 1:300). The mouse anti-beta-gal antibody (Promega) was used at 1:250 dilution, the mouse anti-Elav antibody (Developmental Studies Hybridoma Bank, Iowa) was used at 1:400. Donkey anti-mouse-Cy3 (Jackson Immuno Res. Lab) (dilution 1:1,000) was used as secondary antibody. Larval tissue was checked for Toy protein expression with the anti-Toy antibody (dilution 1:1,000) and donkey anti-rabbit Cy-3 conjugated antibodies (dilution 1:1,500) (Jackson Immuno Res. Lab).
###end p 18
###begin title 19
General procedures and fly stocks
###end title 19
###begin p 20
###xml 135 136 135 136 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</sup>
###xml 198 200 198 200 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">32</sup>
###xml 218 221 218 221 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 382 386 382 386 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR49">2000</xref>
###xml 445 449 445 449 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR39">1994</xref>
5'-RACE of mRNA, PCR, Northern blots and DNA sequencing were carried out according to standard procedures. In the Northern blot poly(A)+ RNA was isolated from 2- to 24-h-old wild-type embryos and a 32P-labeled 1.73 kb toy cDNA was used as probe. RNA size markers were from Promega (RiboMark Labeling). Acridine orange staining was carried out according to standard protocols (Wolff 2000). Embryo staining was done as previously described (Patel 1994). Photos were taken using a Zeiss Axiophot microscope equipped with a CCD camera and KAPPA PS 30 C and KAPPA ImageBase software.
###end p 20
###begin p 21
For the scanning electron microscopy samples were dehydrated in a series of increasing concentrations of ethanol up to 100%, with at least 20 min in every step. They were thereafter dried from liquid carbon dioxide by the critical point technique (Polaron E-3000 Critical Point Drying Apparatus, Polaron Equipment Ltd, Watford, UK). The dried specimens were mounted on aluminum stubs with electrically conductive carbon tape (Agar Scientific, Stansted, UK) and coated with gold using a combined system of sputter coating (Edwards S150A Sputter Coating Unit, Edwards High Vacuum Ltd, Crawley, UK) and a modified evaporation coating system with automatic tilting and rotation device (Edwards E14 Vacuum Coating Unit, Edwards High Vacuum Ltd). Microscopy was performed in a scanning electron microscope (LEO 360ixp SEM, LEO Electron Microscopy Group, Oberkochen, Germany).
###end p 21

###begin p 23
###xml 231 235 201 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 245 247 215 217 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>

###xml 250 253 220 223 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 253 256 223 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>

###xml 260 265 230 235 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 271 274 241 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>

###xml 274 279 244 249 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
###xml 297 301 267 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Gal4</italic>
###xml 316 323 286 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey-Gal4</italic>

###xml 387 393 357 363 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 395 402 365 372 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-P35</italic>
###xml 408 415 378 385 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-GFP</italic>
###xml 490 494 460 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 494 495 464 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;</italic>
###xml 494 495 464 465 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>&#8722;</italic></sup>
###xml 513 514 483 484 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">w</italic>
###xml 516 524 486 494 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-Pax6</italic>
###xml 526 530 496 500 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 530 531 500 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8722;</italic>
###xml 530 531 500 501 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>&#8722;</italic></sup>
###xml 531 534 501 504 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">/ci</italic>
###xml 534 535 504 505 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 534 535 504 505 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 535 538 505 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">spa</italic>
###xml 538 541 508 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pol</italic>
###xml 538 541 508 511 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>pol</italic></sup>
Rescue crosses were done in vials containing standard medium, at the temperatures indicated (29degrees, 25degrees, 22degrees, 18degrees or 15degrees). Each cross was repeated at least once. We analyzed the rescue of four different Pax6 mutants; eyD, toyhdl, eyJ5.71, and toyG7.39. Three different Gal4 driver lines (ey-Gal4 and two toy-Gal4 lines) and five UAS lines (UAS-toy (2 lines), UAS-ey, UAS-P35, and UAS-GFP, which served as a negative control) were used. Frequencies of homozygous Pax6- offspring in the w; UAS-Pax6; Pax6-/ciDspapol stocks were also analyzed after development at different temperatures.
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 11 15 11 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 63 65 63 65 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ci</italic>
###xml 65 66 65 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 65 66 65 66 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 209 211 203 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ci</italic>
###xml 211 212 205 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 211 212 205 206 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
Homozygous Pax6 mutant offspring was identified by lack of the ciD wing phenotype. The rescued offspring was repeatedly tested by crosses to wild-type flies at 25degrees, in order to verify the absence of the ciD marker. In no case the marker chromosome was present. Rescued offspring were scored for phenotype of both compound eyes and ocelli. Flies with smaller than normal eyes, ranging from a discernible loss of peripheral facets to only a single remaining ommatidium, were classified as "small eyes". Presence of all three ocelli and at least one of the 6-8 the interocellar bristles was defined as wild-type ocellar phenotype.
###end p 24

###xml 184 190 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
To be able to compare the wild-type expression pattern and that of the transgenic lines carrying presumptive toy regulatory regions, we generated a Toy-specific polyclonal antibody in rabbit. To test the specificity of this antiserum we over-expressed UAS-toy by introducing a heat-shock driven Gal4 transgene and analyzed the fly proteins with Western blot. Four bands appeared in the w1118 stock (heat shocked) used as control (Fig. 1a). One of these was extremely strong in the heat-shock treated transgenic flies (Fig. 1a, lane 2). The size of the over-expressed protein was in good agreement with the 59-kDa full-length Toy protein. Homozygous toyhdl mutant larvae lacked this band (Fig. 1a, lane 3). The other bands were, however, still present and were, therefore, considered to be due to unspecific binding of the antiserum. We also performed immuno-histochemical analyses of homozygous toyhdl mutant embryos (Fig. 1, compare panels d and e). There was a low level of background staining with the Toy antibody in mutant embryos. The Toy-specific staining in the visual primordia, brain and VNC was, however, missing. Ectopic expression of toy in wing discs using a vg-Gal4 driver gave a strong Toy-signal in a vg-specific manner (Fig. 1i), while wild-type discs showed no Toy staining (not shown).Fig. 1Toy wild-type expression pattern and loss in the toyhdl mutant. a Western blot analysis using the Toy antibody. Lane 1 shows proteins prepared from w1118 adults, heat-shocked by the same regime as the hs-Gal4; UAS-toy adults in lane 2. The Toy protein is visible as a weak band in wild-type, but is strongly over-expressed by heat shock. The arrow indicates the 59-kDa Toy protein. Homozygote toyhdl larvae (lane 3) lack this band, but three weak unrelated bands are still present. b Immunohistochemical staining of Toy in a wild-type embryo (stage 9) showing expression in two circular areas of the head (dorsal view). c Lateral view of a stage 11 wild-type embryo. The Toy-expressing cells have moved dorsally and form an uneven patch, see arrow. d Lateral view of a late stage 13 wild-type embryo. Arrow shows staining at the Bolwig's organ. e Lack of specific staining is observed in a y w; toyhdl embryo (stage 14). Compare with the wild-type expression pattern in d. f Dorsal view of a stage 15 wild-type embryo. Arrows point at the V-shaped eye-antennal primordia. g The reiterated pattern of Toy in the ventral cord of a stage 16 wild-type embryo. h Toy expression pattern in a wild-type eye-antennal disc. i Ectopic expression of Toy in a wing disc using the vg-Gal4 driver
###end p 27

###begin p 29
###xml 276 279 276 279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 344 348 344 348 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 471 472 471 472 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 680 681 680 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 791 792 791 792 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 903 904 903 904 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 965 968 965 968 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1087 1088 1087 1088 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 1209 1212 1209 1212 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1293 1297 1293 1297 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 1318 1322 1318 1322 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR30">2001</xref>
The localization of Toy protein during embryonic and larval development was analyzed using this antiserum. Toy protein was first detected at stage 8 in wild-type embryos (not shown). The initial expression was defined to the posterior procephalic region, i.e., same region as toy transcripts are found with in situ hybridization (Czerny et al. 1999). During embryonic stages 9 and 10, Toy-expressing cells were found in a region covering the ectodermal neuroblasts (Fig. 1b, c). These cells moved dorsally and at stage 13, when neuroblasts invaginate to form the brain, protein staining was seen in the optic lobe primordia and in the larval eye primordium (Bolwig's organ) (Fig. 1d; Supplementary Fig. S1). At stage 15, staining was evident in the primordia of the eye-antennal discs (Fig. 1f). Specific cells in the VNC were visible already at the beginning of stage 14 and at subsequent stages (Fig. 1g). In eye-antennal discs from wild-type third instar larvae toy expression was visible both posterior and anterior to the morphogenetic furrow and in the medial ocellar region (Fig. 1h). The Toy protein expression pattern is thus not completely in agreement with the in situ hybridization results, where toy mRNA is predominately found anterior to the morphogenetic furrow (Czerny et al. 1999; Kammermeier et al. 2001).
###end p 29
###begin title 30
###xml 16 19 16 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
Analyses of the toy regulatory region using Gal4 constructs
###end title 30
###begin p 31
###xml 55 58 55 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 122 125 122 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 231 234 231 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 261 262 261 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 710 713 710 713 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 970 976 970 976 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fig.&#160;2</label>
###xml 1016 1019 1016 1019 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1047 1048 1047 1048 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</bold>
###xml 1092 1095 1092 1095 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1124 1128 1124 1128 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 1132 1133 1132 1133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">6</italic>
###xml 1238 1249 1238 1249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">white boxes</italic>
###xml 1276 1279 1276 1279 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1302 1307 1302 1307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">black</italic>

###xml 1526 1527 1526 1527 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">b</bold>
###xml 1577 1587 1577 1587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1a-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1588 1596 1588 1596 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-LacZ</italic>

In order to identify the cis-regulatory regions of the toy gene, we analyzed the transcription start and the 5' region of toy. An alternative, but rare, transcription start has been found at 954-bp upstream of the earlier reported toy transcription start (Fig. 2a) (Erich Frei, personal communication). This exon (1') is 162-bp long. We sequenced cDNA from embryos and confirmed that this transcription start is used. However, no EST sequence containing this start has been reported. In over-exposed Northern blots, a rare transcript of 1.8 kb was detected, which could correspond to this transcript (not shown). Quantification of the bands showed that the transcript represented approximately 4% of the total toy mRNA in embryos. The cDNA sequence indicated that transcripts initiated at exon 1' are spliced to exon 2 and translated from an AUG site located in exon 3. Translation of this rare transcript would thus result in a Toy protein that lacks the paired domain.Fig. 2Analysis of the 5-kb region upstream of toy using reporter constructs. a Map of the upstream and promoter region of toy showing the Gal4 constructs toy1 to 6. A newly identified transcription start site is marked 1'. The 5' untranslated region is indicated with white boxes and the first part of the toy open reading frame is black. The striped box is translated when spliced to exon 1, but not if transcription starts at exon 1'. Below the map, extents of genomic sequences inserted into Gal4 vectors and used for transformation of flies are shown. b Reporter gene expression in a stage 10 embryo of toy1a-Gal4>UAS-LacZ showing neuroblast expression. c A stage 16 embryo of the same strain showing staining in the embryonic brain and in one eye-antennal primordium (arrow). d A toy1e-Gal4>UAS-LacZ embryo (stage 10) showing an early expression of the lacZ reporter gene. e A toy1a-Gal4>UAS-EGFP eye-antennal disc showing strong expression of the GFP reporter gene in a band anterior to the morphogenetic furrow and in the ocellar region and weak expression in a few spots in the antennal portion
###end p 31

###begin p 33
###xml 94 97 94 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 109 110 109 110 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 114 118 114 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 242 246 242 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 248 252 248 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3</italic>
###xml 258 262 258 262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy4</italic>
###xml 292 296 292 296 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 472 476 472 476 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy5</italic>
###xml 492 496 492 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy6</italic>
Six different promoter constructs were generated in order to dissect the 5' regulation of the toy gene (Fig. 2a). toy1 contained 5,203 bp of genomic DNA upstream and 526 bp downstream of the canonical transcription start (exon 1). Constructs toy2, toy3, and toy4 had the same proximal end as toy1 but contained 767, 597, and 320 bp of upstream DNA, respectively. Two constructs contained the region upstream of and including the alternative transcription start (exon 1'); toy5 (4,457 bp) and toy6 (1,313 bp).
###end p 33
###begin p 34
###xml 115 127 115 127 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-RpL14.IR</italic>
###xml 229 236 229 236 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey-Gal4</italic>
###xml 285 287 285 287 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 433 437 433 437 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR14">2003</xref>
###xml 500 503 500 503 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 503 506 503 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 503 506 503 506 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 510 512 510 512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 512 513 512 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 512 513 512 513 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 616 619 616 619 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 680 684 680 684 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 689 693 689 693 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 747 756 747 756 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-RpL14</italic>
###xml 756 760 756 760 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RNAi</italic>
###xml 756 760 756 760 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>RNAi</italic></sup>
###xml 1054 1059 1054 1059 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">white</italic>
###xml 1059 1060 1059 1060 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</italic>
###xml 1059 1060 1059 1060 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>+</italic></sup>
###xml 1136 1145 1136 1145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-RpL14</italic>
###xml 1145 1149 1145 1149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RNAi</italic>
###xml 1145 1149 1145 1149 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>RNAi</italic></sup>
###xml 1207 1216 1207 1216 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-RpL14</italic>
###xml 1216 1220 1216 1220 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">RNAi</italic>
###xml 1216 1220 1216 1220 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>RNAi</italic></sup>
###xml 1317 1321 1317 1321 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
The regulatory function of the constructs was first analyzed by crossing transformed lines to a stock containing a UAS-RpL14.IR transgene. This is an RNAi construct of the Ribosomal protein L14. By driving this construct with an ey-Gal4 driver (containing the eye-specific enhancer of ey) Lambertsson and co-workers were able to generate headless flies due to interference with the translational machinery in the head (Enerly et al. 2003). This phenotype is very similar to the headless phenotype of toyhdl or eyD homozygotes. The results from these crosses are summarized in Supplementary Table S1. The two longest toy-promoter regions containing the exon 1 transcription start (toy1 and toy2) resulted in lethality (4 of 11 lines) together with UAS-RpL14RNAi and a headless phenotype of pharate adults (dissected out of the pupal cases) was found in two of these lines. The variation in phenotype between lines of a specific construct indicated position effects at the transgene insertion sites, a notion strengthened by the variable expression of the white+ reporter gene, which was variegated or very weak in most lines viable with UAS-RpL14RNAi. None of the other tested constructs gave lethality with UAS-RpL14RNAi, indicating that a DNA region of at least 1.3 kb surrounding the canonical transcription start (toy2) is important for correct Toy expression during head development.
###end p 34
###begin p 35
###xml 44 52 44 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy-Gal4</italic>
###xml 83 91 83 91 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-lacZ</italic>
###xml 96 103 96 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-GFP</italic>
###xml 267 271 267 271 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">lacZ</italic>
###xml 325 329 322 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 334 338 331 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 375 379 372 376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">lacZ</italic>
###xml 399 400 396 397 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 445 446 442 443 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 518 521 515 518 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 535 539 532 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3</italic>
###xml 607 611 604 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy4</italic>
###xml 878 882 875 879 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 884 889 881 886 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2,</italic>
###xml 894 898 891 895 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3</italic>
###xml 977 981 974 978 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">LacZ</italic>
###xml 1035 1039 1032 1036 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy5</italic>
###xml 1044 1048 1041 1045 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy6</italic>
We also crossed a portion of the transgenic toy-Gal4 lines to reporter constructs (UAS-lacZ and UAS-GFP) to analyze the embryonic, larval, and adult expression patterns. The results are summarized in Supplementary Table S1. The embryonic expression was analyzed with lacZ staining using an anti-betagal antibody. Many of the toy1 and toy2 lines showed specific expression of lacZ in the brain (Fig. 2b-e) and in the eye-antennal primordia (Fig. 2c, only one primordium is in focus) resembling the normal expression of toy. One of five toy3 lines also showed this expression pattern. The shortest construct (toy4) and the two constructs using the upstream transcription start did not give this pattern, indicating that an embryonic eye-antennal specific enhancer is located within the 1,123-bp-region surrounding the canonical transcription start site. VNC staining was found in toy1, toy2, and toy3 lines, but not with the other transgenic constructs. We also found unexpected LacZ stainings in some lines, e.g., expression of all the toy5 and toy6 Gal4 driver constructs was confined to one pair of cells in the ventral part of the head during early embryogenesis. Other lines stained cells in the amnioserrosa and cells reminiscent of embryonic hemocytes. The latter patterns were not consistent between lines of a specific construct and were therefore considered as caused by position effects.
###end p 35
###begin p 36
###xml 42 45 42 45 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 205 209 205 209 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 211 215 211 215 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 217 222 217 222 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3,</italic>
###xml 227 231 227 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy4</italic>
###xml 350 359 350 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1-Gal4</italic>
###xml 366 367 366 367 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 374 383 374 383 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2-Gal4</italic>
###xml 497 501 497 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy3</italic>
###xml 506 510 506 510 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy4</italic>
###xml 783 787 783 787 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 791 795 791 795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
We also analyzed larval expression of the toy regulatory constructs in the eye-antennal imaginal discs and brains. These results are summarized in Supplementary Table S1. The regulatory regions present in toy1, toy2, toy3, and toy4 constructs induced GFP expression in eye-antennal discs (5 of 17 lines) and/or in brain (5 of 17 lines). The discs of toy1-Gal4 (Fig. 2e) and toy2-Gal4 show GFP expression anterior to the morphogenetic furrow, resembling the Toy wild-type expression pattern, while toy3 and toy4 gave signals only at the posterior edge of the eye disc (Supplementary Fig. S2). The other tested transgenic lines showed no fluorescence in either discs or brain. Furthermore, exterior examination of GFP expression revealed fluorescence in brains of adult flies carrying toy1 or toy2 constructs (4 of 5 lines tested).
###end p 36
###begin p 37
###xml 25 28 25 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 53 68 53 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. melanogaster</italic>
###xml 73 89 73 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. pseudoobscura</italic>
###xml 204 208 204 208 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR35">2003</xref>
###xml 357 367 357 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 387 399 387 399 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">melanogaster</italic>
###xml 404 411 404 411 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">obscura</italic>
###xml 476 486 476 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">willistoni</italic>
###xml 488 496 488 496 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">virilis,</italic>
###xml 501 508 501 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">repleta</italic>
###xml 608 615 608 615 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eyeless</italic>
###xml 693 696 693 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 53 68 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 73 89 <span type="species:ncbi:7237">D. pseudoobscura</span>
###xml 143 148 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
Alignment studies of the toy upstream region between D. melanogaster and D. pseudoobscura did not reveal much conservation. However, using the human Pax6 consensus binding site in ConSite (Lenhard et al. 2003) we identified two putative Pax6-binding sites flanking the canonical transcription start site. These sites were conserved in seven closely related Drosophila species within the melanogaster and obscura groups, but they were not present in the more distantly related willistoni, virilis, and repleta groups. Neither were they present at the transcription start site or in the coding sequence of the eyeless gene. We also noted a presumptive Bicoid binding site 250 bp upstream of the toy transcription start.
###end p 37
###begin p 38
###xml 362 366 362 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1</italic>
###xml 371 375 371 375 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2</italic>
###xml 443 446 443 446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 451 453 451 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 491 495 491 495 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 505 508 505 508 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 508 511 508 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 508 511 508 511 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 513 516 513 516 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 516 521 516 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G7.39</italic>
###xml 516 521 516 521 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
###xml 523 525 523 525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 525 530 525 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 525 530 525 530 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 535 537 535 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 537 538 537 538 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 537 538 537 538 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
In summary, the results indicate that a 1.3-kb region surrounding the transcription start site is important for correct Toy expression during embryonic and larval development. However, transcription from the alternative transcription start site (exon 1'), does not seem to play a major role for the expression of Toy and was not studied further. With the use of toy1 and toy2 Gal4 driver constructs we set out to induce targeted expression of toy and ey cDNAs in order to rescue some strong Pax6 mutants (toyhdl, toyG7.39, eyJ5.71 and eyD).
###end p 38
###begin title 39
###xml 10 13 10 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
Rescue of toy mutants
###end title 39
###begin p 40
###xml 52 55 52 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 55 58 55 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 55 58 55 58 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 218 222 218 222 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 571 575 559 563 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 746 747 734 735 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 786 787 774 775 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 845 848 833 836 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 848 851 836 839 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 848 851 836 839 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 907 910 895 898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1080 1083 1068 1071 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1083 1086 1071 1074 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 1083 1086 1071 1074 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 1111 1112 1099 1100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 1154 1157 1142 1145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1157 1160 1145 1148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 1157 1160 1145 1148 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 1194 1197 1182 1185 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1197 1202 1185 1190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G7.39</italic>
###xml 1197 1202 1185 1190 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
###xml 1217 1221 1205 1209 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR43">2002</xref>
###xml 1281 1284 1269 1272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1284 1287 1272 1275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 1284 1287 1272 1275 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 1425 1428 1413 1416 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1428 1433 1416 1421 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G7.39</italic>
###xml 1428 1433 1416 1421 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
###xml 1516 1519 1504 1507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1519 1524 1507 1512 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G7.39</italic>
###xml 1519 1524 1507 1512 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
As shown earlier, about one-third of the homozygous toyhdl mutants die during embryonal or larval stages and the remaining two-thirds reach the pupal stage, where many develop as far as pharate adults (Kronhamn et al. 2002). At this stage they die since they are unable to escape from the pupal case. Almost no escapers eclose at 25degrees or at higher temperatures. If balance stocks are allowed to grow at 18degrees, about 3% of the eclosing flies are homozygous mutant with normal head morphology, apart from the ocelli, which are aberrant or missing (Kronhamn et al. 2002). Removal of the pupal cases shows flies with variable head defects, ranging from almost normal heads with small compound eyes, over "half-heads" and "cleft-heads" (Fig. 4f), to completely headless flies (Fig. 4h) where the proboscis is protruding from the thorax. The toyhdl mutant is caused by a deletion uncovering exons 6-9 of toy. This would theoretically result in a protein with a truncated homeodomain but with an intact paired domain. Antibody staining, however, showed no protein in homozygote toyhdl embryos or larvae (Fig. 1). For the rescue experiments we used the toyhdl allele and a hypomorphic allele; toyG7.39 (Punzo et al. 2002), which also exhibits a headless phenotype very similar to toyhdl homozygotes. Staining with the Toy antibody showed that Toy protein is below detection level in the eye-antennal primordia of homozygous toyG7.39 embryos; however, we found expression in the VNC (not shown), indicating that the toyG7.39 mutant is an eye-specific allele.
###end p 40

To optimize the temperature sensitivity property of the Gal4/UAS system (Jarrett 2000) flies are normally raised at 29degrees (Brand and Perrimon 1993), which provides a balance between maximal Gal4 activity and minimal detrimental effects on fertility and viability. However, at this temperature the effect of driver and/or responder was so strong that no flies survived (Fig. 3). By decreasing the developmental temperature to 25degrees, we found an eclosion rate of rescued homozygous toyhdl flies of about 3.5% (Fig. 3, black bar) compared to 4% in flies without rescuing transgenes (light gray bar) and 0.9% in balanced stocks (white bar). The survival was, thus, not significantly different with or without rescuing constructs. Neither did we find any significant rescue at 22degrees. At 18degrees and 15degrees, however, the frequency of eclosing homozygotes increased significantly to about 20-23% in flies carrying both toy-Gal4 (toy1a or toy2b) and UAS-toy constructs (Fig. 3, black bars). The expected frequency of toyhdl/toyhdl adults at full rescue was 33%. Unexpectedly, we found an equally high rescue level of homozygouos toyhdl flies carrying the UAS-toy construct alone (dark gray bars). The experiments were repeated with five different toy-Gal4 lines and two different UAS-toy lines, and in all cases the rescue of toyhdl homozygotes was comparable, irrespective of whether the toy-Gal4 driver was present or not. The rescue at these lower temperatures was, however, significantly higher than the number of homozygotes without UAS-toy constructs (Fig. 3, white, light gray and medium gray bars). The results also indicated that there was a positive effect on survival obtained by just crossing flies, since the classes of offspring carrying no construct or only toy-Gal4 also showed a weak increase in survival compared to balanced stocks at some temperatures. This effect was, however, not found when we examined survival of toyhdl homozygotes carrying toy1a-Gal4>UAS-GFP. The number of viable adult offspring in these crosses was not significantly different from the level of escapers in the w; toyhdl/ciDspapol stock (not shown), indicating that toy-Gal4 did not cause rescue by itself. Using the same construct (toy1a-Gal4>UAS-toy) we were also able to rescue homozygous toyG7.39 mutant flies with similar efficiencies as the toyhdl mutant (Table 1 and not shown). To explore whether the UAS-toy transgene was transcribed also without a Gal4 driver construct, we made quantitative RT-PCR analyses of flies carrying the UAS-toy with and without driver in a toyhdl background (Supplementary Fig. S3). The flies reared at 25degrees showed increased levels of toy transcripts whenever UAS-toy was present (also without a toy-Gal4 driver construct). In these flies we also observed a weak increase in ey transcription. The results indicate that the UAS-toy construct used was leaking.Fig. 3Rescue from lethality of toyhdl homozygotes with toy-Gal4>UAS-toy at different developmental temperatures. Significant rescue compared to controls (chi2 test; P < 0.001) was obtained at 15degrees and 18degrees with toy-Gal4>UAS-toy but also with UAS-toy alone. The figures are based on the total of toy1a and toy2b rescue cross results since these figures did not differ significantly. Apart from the increase in survival of homozygous toy mutant flies, we also found an improvement of the ocellar phenotypes of the rescued flies when combining toy-Gal4 with UAS-toy (Table 1; Fig. 4a, b). A similar rescue of the ocelli formation was found in flies carrying the UAS-toy construct alone, while flies only carrying the driver still lacked ocelli. The proportion of flies with normal ocelli among the homozygous escapers in a toyhdl/ciDspapol stock was 18% at 18degrees. However, in rescued flies, this proportion increased to 50%. The ocellar phenotype of toyG7.39 mutant homozygotes was weaker (71% normal flies) than that of toyhdl, but a phenotypic improvement was achieved with an exogenous expression of UAS-toy (Table 1).Fig. 4Scanning electron micrographs of heads from toy and ey mutants and rescued flies. a Rescue of homozygous toyG7.39 with toy1f-Gal4>UAS-toy. The phenotype is indistinguishable from wild type. The interocellar bristles are marked with an arrowhead. b Rescue of toyhdl with toy1a-Gal4>UAS-toy. The ocellar phenotype is classified as wild type since it has three ocelli and a few interocellar bristles in the correct positions. c Rescue of eyD with ey-Gal4>UAS-ey. d Rescue of homozygous toyG7.39 with the anti-apoptotic protein P35 (toy2b-Gal4>UAS-P35). Compound eyes are wild type, but ocelli are missing. e Rescue of eyD with P35 (ey-Gal4>UAS-P35). Compound eyes are missing, but ocelli are normal. a-e All flies have all eclosed from the pupal case. f A homozygous toyhdl pharate adult showing a weaker head phenotype "cleft head". g Homozygous headless eyD pharate adult. h Homozygous headless toyhdl pharate adult. f-h Pharate adults dissected out of the pupal cases. a-e, g are the same scale. Bars 200 mum
###end p 49

###xml 130 137 130 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 235 244 235 244 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">arrowhead</italic>
