###xml 423 424 423 424 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">c</bold>
###xml 435 437 435 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 437 438 437 438 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 437 438 437 438 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 444 458 444 458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey-Gal4&gt;UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 460 461 460 461 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</bold>
###xml 483 486 483 486 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 486 491 486 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G7.39</italic>
###xml 486 491 486 491 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
###xml 529 539 529 539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy2b-Gal4</italic>
###xml 540 547 540 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-P35</italic>
###xml 603 604 603 604 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e</bold>
###xml 615 617 615 617 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 617 618 617 618 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 617 618 617 618 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 629 644 629 644 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey-Gal4&gt;UAS-P35</italic>
###xml 697 698 697 698 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</bold>
###xml 699 700 699 700 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e</bold>
###xml 749 750 749 750 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">f</bold>
###xml 764 767 764 767 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 767 770 767 770 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 767 770 767 770 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 831 832 831 832 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</bold>
###xml 853 855 853 855 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 855 856 855 856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 855 856 855 856 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 872 873 872 873 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">h</bold>
###xml 894 897 894 897 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 897 900 897 900 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 897 900 897 900 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 916 917 916 917 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">f</bold>
###xml 918 919 918 919 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">h</bold>
###xml 969 970 969 970 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</bold>
###xml 971 972 971 972 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e</bold>
###xml 974 975 974 975 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">g</bold>
###xml 996 1000 996 1000 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Bars</italic>
Scanning electron micrographs of heads from toy and ey mutants and rescued flies. a Rescue of homozygous toyG7.39 with toy1f-Gal4>UAS-toy. The phenotype is indistinguishable from wild type. The interocellar bristles are marked with an arrowhead. b Rescue of toyhdl with toy1a-Gal4>UAS-toy. The ocellar phenotype is classified as wild type since it has three ocelli and a few interocellar bristles in the correct positions. c Rescue of eyD with ey-Gal4>UAS-ey. d Rescue of homozygous toyG7.39 with the anti-apoptotic protein P35 (toy2b-Gal4>UAS-P35). Compound eyes are wild type, but ocelli are missing. e Rescue of eyD with P35 (ey-Gal4>UAS-P35). Compound eyes are missing, but ocelli are normal. a-e All flies have all eclosed from the pupal case. f A homozygous toyhdl pharate adult showing a weaker head phenotype "cleft head". g Homozygous headless eyD pharate adult. h Homozygous headless toyhdl pharate adult. f-h Pharate adults dissected out of the pupal cases. a-e, g are the same scale. Bars 200 mum
###end p 50
###begin p 51
###xml 105 108 105 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 148 155 148 155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 277 284 265 272 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 392 400 380 388 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy-Gal4</italic>
###xml 459 462 447 450 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 462 465 450 453 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 462 465 450 453 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
To conclude, we obtained a significant amelioration of the survival and the head phenotype of homozygous toy mutant flies with a transgenic copy of UAS-toy at lower temperatures (15degrees and 18degrees) while at higher temperatures survival was not improved. We find that the UAS-toy transgenic construct can induce transcription of its own at higher temperatures. Thus, the presence of the toy-Gal4 driver construct is not necessary to obtain rescue of the toyhdl mutant. However, at higher temperatures the Toy levels probably are too high to promote development.
###end p 51
###begin title 52
###xml 9 11 9 11 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 11 12 11 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 11 12 11 12 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
Recue of eyD
###end title 52
###begin p 53
###xml 35 37 35 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 94 96 94 96 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 96 97 96 97 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 96 97 96 97 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 175 177 175 177 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 202 206 202 206 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">1998</xref>
###xml 223 227 223 227 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR43">2002</xref>
###xml 259 261 259 261 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 261 266 261 266 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 261 266 261 266 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 280 294 280 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey-Gal4&gt;UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 300 302 300 302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 302 307 302 307 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 302 307 302 307 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 438 442 438 442 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR42">2001</xref>
###xml 450 452 450 452 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 452 457 452 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 452 457 452 457 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 462 464 462 464 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 464 465 464 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 464 465 464 465 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 504 506 504 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 506 511 506 511 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 506 511 506 511 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 545 547 545 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 547 548 547 548 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 547 548 547 548 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 561 563 561 563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 563 568 563 568 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 563 568 563 568 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 664 666 664 666 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 666 667 666 667 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 666 667 666 667 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 779 781 779 781 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 802 806 802 806 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR4">1997</xref>
###xml 822 826 822 826 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">1998</xref>
###xml 845 851 845 851 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 900 902 900 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 902 903 902 903 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 902 903 902 903 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 923 924 923 924 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 1078 1080 1078 1080 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1080 1081 1080 1081 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 1080 1081 1080 1081 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 1096 1097 1096 1097 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 1132 1133 1132 1133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 1155 1158 1155 1158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1158 1161 1158 1161 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 1158 1161 1158 1161 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 1204 1206 1204 1206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1206 1207 1206 1207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1206 1207 1206 1207 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 1313 1315 1295 1297 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1315 1316 1297 1298 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1315 1316 1297 1298 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 1369 1383 1351 1365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey-Gal4&gt;UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 1414 1420 1396 1402 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-ey</italic>
It has been shown that full-length ey cDNA is able to efficiently rescue the eye phenotype in ey2 mutants when expressed in the eye disc under the control of the eye-specific ey enhancer (Halder et al. 1998). Punzo et al. (2002) also reported a rescue of the eyJ5.71 allele using ey-Gal4>UAS-ey. The eyJ5.71 allele is caused by a 9-kb deletion in the 5' region of the gene and is described as an RNA and protein null mutant (Punzo et al. 2001). Both eyJ5.71 and eyD mutations cause homozygous lethality (eyJ5.71 to 81%); however, in contrast to eyD, homozygous eyJ5.71 adults are not headless. First, we wanted to test whether it was possible to rescue homozygous eyD pharates by targeted expressing of Ey. Using a driver construct consisting of the eye-specific enhancer of the ey gene (Bonini et al. 1997; Halder et al. 1998) combined with an UAS-ey transgene, we were able to significantly rescue eyD homozygotes (Table 1). The flies that eclosed from pupae exhibited smaller than normal heads and a majority of the compound eyes were rescued to a size comparable to that of ey2 mutants (Fig. 4c) while ocelli were normal (Table 1). As observed in the toyhdl rescue, we found that viability rescue of eyD was more efficient at 18degrees compared to 25degrees and 29degrees and also that rescue efficiencies of eyD flies carrying both driver and effector constructs (ey-Gal4>UAS-ey) or effector construct alone (UAS-ey) were similar (not shown). This was found for both survival and compound eye phenotype.
###end p 53
###begin p 54
###xml 157 159 157 159 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 159 160 159 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 159 160 159 160 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 205 207 205 207 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 230 234 230 234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR43">2002</xref>
To conclude, the results show that exogenous expression of Ey can partially rescue both lethality and compound eye structure of the dominant-negative mutant eyD, in analogy with previous results for other ey mutants (Punzo et al. 2002).
###end p 54
###begin title 55
Toy and Ey can substitute for each other but have distinct functions in head formation
###end title 55
###begin p 56
###xml 81 84 81 84 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 100 104 100 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 179 181 179 181 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 215 219 215 219 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR44">2004</xref>
###xml 227 230 227 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 235 237 235 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 389 400 389 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">sine oculis</italic>
###xml 463 467 463 467 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR43">2002</xref>
###xml 643 647 643 647 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 792 795 792 795 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 800 802 800 802 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
Targeted expression of Ey can induce ectopic eye formation, without induction of toy (Czerny et al. 1999). Moreover, it has been shown that Toy can activate eye development in an ey-independent manner (Punzo et al. 2004). Both toy and ey are expressed in the embryonic eye primordium and later on in the eye-antennal discs. Furthermore, both proteins regulate the eye-specific enhancer of sine oculis, by binding to partly overlapping binding sites (Punzo et al. 2002). In spite of the fact that there are differences in the expression patterns in brain, VNC and in the ocellar territory of the eye discs, these findings indicate that the two Pax6 genes act in parallel and have redundant functions in eye development. To investigate such a redundancy, we set up crosses to rescue homozygous toy and ey mutants, respectively, through ectopic expression of the paralogous Pax6 protein.
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 53 56 53 56 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 56 59 56 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 56 59 56 59 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 84 90 84 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 123 130 123 130 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 152 162 152 162 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1a-Gal4</italic>
###xml 177 178 177 178 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 203 206 203 206 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 206 211 206 211 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G7.39</italic>
###xml 206 211 206 211 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G7.39</italic></sup>
###xml 262 268 262 268 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 279 282 279 282 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 364 366 364 366 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 366 367 366 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 366 367 366 367 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 409 427 409 427 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy1a-Gal4&gt;UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 443 457 443 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey-Gal4&gt;UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 486 487 486 487 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 512 515 512 515 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 523 525 523 525 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 525 530 525 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 525 530 525 530 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 603 604 597 598 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 624 626 618 620 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 626 631 620 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 626 631 620 625 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 679 686 673 680 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 694 695 688 689 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab1" ref-type="table">1</xref>
###xml 741 743 735 737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 743 744 737 738 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 743 744 737 738 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 797 800 791 794 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 888 890 882 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 890 891 884 885 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 890 891 884 885 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
We found that the rescue from pupal lethality of the toyhdl mutant by expression of UAS-ey was as effective as rescue with UAS-toy (14%) when using the toy1a-Gal4 driver (Table 1). Also, the survival of toyG7.39 homozygotes was improved by ectopic expression of UAS-ey. For both toy mutants, the ocellar phenotype was partially rescued. Furthermore, the rescue of eyD homozygotes was even more efficient with toy1a-Gal4>UAS-toy (7%) than with ey-Gal4>UAS-ey over-expression (3%) (Table 1). Ectopic expression of toy in the eyJ5.71 mutant also gave a significantly increased survival at 18degrees (Table 1). Compound eyes of eyJ5.71 homozygotes were fully restored by one copy of UAS-toy (Table 1). The morphology of compound eyes in rescued eyD mutants was also improved by targeted expression of toy, but never to wild-type proportions. A small eye phenotype was found in 76% of rescued eyD flies, while without rescue the rare surviving homozygous flies never develop compound eyes. All these experiments were also performed at 22degrees with similar results (not shown).
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 25 28 25 28 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 88 90 88 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 90 95 90 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 90 95 90 95 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 162 164 162 164 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 180 187 180 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 189 192 189 192 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 192 195 192 195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 192 195 192 195 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 222 229 222 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 231 233 231 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 233 238 233 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 233 238 233 238 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 287 289 287 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 289 294 289 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 289 294 289 294 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 332 335 332 335 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 465 469 465 469 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR44">2004</xref>
To verify that increased toy levels did not inadvertently induce transcription from the eyJ5.71 gene, we made RT-PRC analyses. We found a significant increase of ey mRNA levels in UAS-toy; toyhdl flies, but no increase in UAS-toy; eyJ5.71 flies (Supplementary Fig. S3). We conclude that eyJ5.71 is not induced by over-expression of toy, indicating that Toy protein can promote head and eye development in an Ey-independent manner, as proposed earlier (Punzo et al. 2004).
###end p 58
###begin p 59
In summary, Pax6 proteins can substitute for each other concerning both head structures and survival. However, rescue is only partial; indicating either that the proteins are not completely interchangeable or that the levels of expression and the spatial and temporal requirements are not adequately reproduced by the artificial Gal4-UAS system.
###end p 59
###begin title 60
###xml 32 35 32 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
Cell death in imaginal discs of toy mutants and rescue with P35
###end title 60
###begin p 61
###xml 5 7 5 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 7 8 7 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 7 8 7 8 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 13 16 13 16 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 16 19 16 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 16 19 16 19 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 83 87 83 87 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 210 213 210 213 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 256 258 256 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 329 333 329 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 517 520 517 520 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 520 523 520 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 520 523 520 523 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 528 530 528 530 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 530 531 530 531 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 530 531 530 531 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
Both eyD and toyhdl homozyogous mutants have a headless phenotype (Kronhamn et al. 2002) which results in pupal lethality. The eye phenotypes of the escaping or rescued flies are, however, very different, with toy mutants exhibiting defective ocelli while ey mutants lack or have small compound eyes. This indicates that neither Pax6 gene can substitute for the other completely but display a certain degree of subfunctionality. To further corroborate this difference, we analyzed morphology of eye-antennal discs in toyhdl and eyD mutant larvae and stained the discs with acridine orange to examine levels and localization of cell death.
###end p 61
###begin p 62
###xml 40 43 40 43 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 43 46 43 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>

When dissecting eye-antennal discs from toyhdl homozygous larvae grown at 21degrees, the variability of disc morphology was striking. Fully normal eye-antennal discs were found, as well as defects ranging from size reduction, deformation (Fig. 5c, d), lack of parts (Fig. 5e, f) to complete loss of discs. Asymmetric loss of disc portions was often seen. To verify which part of the discs was missing, we used the neuronal marker alpha-Elav, which stains the differentiated neurons in the eye portion of the disc. In Fig. 5f, a pair of eye-antennal discs from a homozygous toyhdl third instar larva is shown where the antennal part of one disc is completely missing and the eye portion is smaller. Duplications of the antennal disc were also observed. The frequency of defects was in good agreement with the phenotypes of pharate adults found at this temperature (Kronhamn et al. 2002).Fig. 5Toy expression and cell death in eye-antennal discs. a Acridine orange (AO) staining of a wild-type eye-antennal disc. Arrow points at the morphogenetic furrow in the eye disc. b Eye-antennal disc from a homozygous eyD mutant larva showing a strongly reduced eye portion (right part) with high levels of cell death. c, d Eye-antennal discs from two homozygous toyhdl mutant larvae with almost wild-type phenotype except an increased level of cell death in the posterior part of the antennal portion. e A homozygous toyhdl disc showing complete loss of the antennal portion and increased levels of cell death in the anterior part of the eye portion. f alpha-Elav staining of a pair of eye-antennal discs from a homozygous toyhdl mutant larva showing asymmetric loss of one antennal portion and size reduction of the eye portion. All discs are third instar larval eye-antennal discs with anterior to the left

###xml 53 54 53 54 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</bold>

###begin p 64
###xml 131 132 131 132 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig5" ref-type="fig">5</xref>
###xml 247 250 247 250 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 250 253 250 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 250 253 250 253 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 437 438 431 432 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig5" ref-type="fig">5</xref>
###xml 641 642 635 636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig5" ref-type="fig">5</xref>
###xml 673 675 667 669 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 675 676 669 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 675 676 669 670 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 799 800 793 794 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig5" ref-type="fig">5</xref>
###xml 867 869 861 863 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 869 870 863 864 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 869 870 863 864 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 894 898 888 892 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">1998</xref>
Staining of wild-type eye-antennal discs with acridine orange revealed a low level of cell death in the eye part as expected (Fig. 5a). In the antennal portion, these larvae showed small discrete regions of acridine orange staining. In homozygous toyhdl larvae staining was relatively normal in the eye portion of most discs at 21degrees. In the antennal part of the discs, on the other hand, massive cell death was often observed (Fig. 5c, d). In cases where the antennal part was gone, cell death seemed to spread into the anterior edge of the eye portion reaching the region where the frons and ocelli precursor cells are localized (Fig. 5e). We also stained discs from eyD homozygous larvae and found a massive cell death which was most prominent in the remaining portion of the eye discs (Fig. 5b). This is comparable to the acridine orange staining reported in ey2 mutants (Halder et al. 1998).
###end p 64
###begin p 65
###xml 120 124 120 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">1994</xref>

###xml 1307 1310 1301 1304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 1307 1310 1301 1304 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 1304 1310 1298 1304 <td xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" align="left" rowspan="3"><italic>toy</italic><sup><italic>hdl</italic></sup></td>
###xml 1310 1311 1304 1305 <td xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" align="left">&#8211;</td>
###xml 1311 1315 1305 1309 <td xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" char="." align="char">3.75</td>

###xml 1304 1319 1298 1313 <tr xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><td align="left" rowspan="3"><italic>toy</italic><sup><italic>hdl</italic></sup></td><td align="left">&#8211;</td><td char="." align="char">3.75</td><td char="." align="char">1013</td></tr>

Statistical analyses were made with &#967;<sup>2</sup>-test, comparing with the frequency of escapers without rescuing construct</p><p textid="68">***&#160;<italic>P</italic>&#160;&lt;&#160;0.001</p></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
We have previously shown that targeted expression of the baculovirus P35 protein, an inhibitor of apoptosis (Hay et al. 1994; Wolff 2000), could rescue the pupal lethality of eyD homozygotes (Kronhamn et al. 2002). Since we found a considerable amount of cell death in the eye-antennal imaginal discs in homozygous toyhdl larvae, we investigated whether apoptosis inhibition could rescue also the toy mutant phenotypes. We expressed P35 protein under the shorter toy promoter, toy2b-Gal4>UAS-P35, in homozygous toyhdl and toyG7.39 flies, respectively, and found that it was possible to significantly increase survival of both mutants (Table 2 and not shown). In contrast to the results with UAS-toy, however, we found that the ocellar defects of the rescued flies did not improve (Fig. 4d). Another difference was that both driver (toy-Gal4) and effector (UAS-P35) had to be present to increase survival (Table 2). For comparison, we repeated the P35-induced rescue of eyD and obtained an increase in viability (Table 2) and improved head structures (except compound eyes) (Fig. 4, compare e and g) as previously reported (Kronhamn et al. 2002).Table 2Rescue of lethality of Pax6 mutants with exogenous P35 (18degrees)MutantRescuing constructFraction of homozygote adults (%)aTotal no of offspring scoredtoyhdl-3.751013UAS-P356.57137toy2b-Gal4; UAS-P3519.6***133toyG7.39-5.10471UAS-P358.48672toy2b-Gal4; UAS-P3516.6***295eyD-0.27366UAS-P35042ey-Gal4; UAS-P3515.6***122aObserved fraction of viable flies homozygous for the Pax6 mutation (i.e., lacking the ciDspapol chromosome). The expected fraction of homozygous adults at full rescue was 33%. Statistical analyses were made with chi2-test, comparing with the frequency of escapers without rescuing construct*** P < 0.001
###end p 65

###xml 23 27 23 27 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
Rescue of lethality of Pax6 mutants with exogenous P35 (18degrees)
###end p 66
###begin p 67
###xml 0 1 0 1 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">a</sup>
###xml 54 58 54 58 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>

###xml 89 90 89 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>

###xml 90 93 90 93 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">spa</italic>

###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 56 59 56 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 64 66 64 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 66 67 66 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 66 67 66 67 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
These results indicate that the pupal lethality of both toy and eyD mutants is caused by cell loss due to apoptosis, and that inhibition of cell death can improve head structures sufficiently for the pharate adults to escape from the pupal shell. The visual system phenotypes are, however, not rescued by inhibition of apoptosis.
###end p 69
###begin title 70
Discussion
###end title 70
###begin p 71
###xml 22 25 22 25 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 27 29 27 29 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 31 34 31 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eya</italic>
###xml 36 39 36 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eyg</italic>
###xml 41 44 41 44 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">dac</italic>
###xml 46 52 46 52 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">optix,</italic>
###xml 57 60 57 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">tsh</italic>
###xml 77 81 77 81 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">1995</xref>
###xml 97 101 97 101 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 117 121 117 121 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR4">1997</xref>
###xml 135 139 135 139 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR25">2003</xref>
###xml 157 161 157 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR46">1997</xref>
###xml 183 187 183 187 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR45">2000</xref>
###xml 203 207 203 207 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR38">1998</xref>
###xml 279 289 279 289 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
To date, seven genes (toy, ey, eya, eyg, dac, optix, and tsh) (Halder et al. 1995; Czerny et al. 1999; Bonini et al. 1997: Jang et al. 2003; Shen and Mardon 1997; Seimiya and Gehring 2000; Pan and Rubin 1998) have been considered to be important factors for eye specification in Drosophila. All of them could be called "master control gene of eye development" since it is possible to induce ectopic eyes by misexpression of any of them. Genetic and molecular studies show that these proteins do not lie in a linear biochemical pathway, but rather form an elaborate regulatory network. Our results strengthen this picture since we find that Ey can partially substitute for Toy and vice versa.
###end p 71
###begin title 72
###xml 12 15 12 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
Alternative toy transcription start
###end title 72
###begin p 73
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 249 253 249 253 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 436 440 436 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR15">1994</xref>
###xml 556 560 556 560 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR27">1997</xref>
###xml 566 576 566 576 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C. elegans</italic>
###xml 726 730 726 730 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR50">1995</xref>
###xml 747 751 747 751 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR42">2001</xref>
###xml 982 985 982 985 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 994 1004 994 1004 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 1141 1145 1141 1145 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy5</italic>
###xml 1151 1155 1151 1155 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy6</italic>
###xml 1156 1160 1156 1160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Gal4</italic>
###xml 566 576 <span type="species:ncbi:6239">C. elegans</span>
Pax6 genes encode nuclear transcription factors, which are characterized by two structurally conserved DNA-binding domains: the paired domain and the paired-like homeodomain. Vertebrates often possess multiple protein isoforms derived from a single Pax6 gene, which can result in distinct expression in different tissues. In mammals, the Pax6(5a) isoform, containing a variant Paired domain with altered DNA recognition (Epstein et al. 1994) has been detected predominantly in eye tissue, while other isoforms are expressed more generally (Jaworski et al. 1997). In C. elegans, an isoform of Pax6, without the paired domain, was found to be important for correct development of the peripheral nervous system (Zhang and Emmons 1995). Punzo et al. (2001) reported that the homeodomain of the Ey protein is dispensable for eye development in flies, but instead have a repressive property directed against the Distal-less protein. The discovery of a new transcription start site in the toy gene in Drosophila, which could be translated into a protein lacking the paired domain, is therefore of interest. The analyses of its expression using the toy5- and toy6-Gal4 driver constructs highlighted a single pair of cells, which seemed to be in contact with the VNC in the posterior part of the embryonic head and could possibly cluster with the labial sensory complex important for formation of the peripheral nervous system of the head. This transcript is, however, not extensively expressed and we are reluctant to ascribe this alternative transcription start site any vital importance in eye or CNS formation.
###end p 73
###begin title 74
###xml 34 37 34 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
The 5-kb cis-regulatory region of toy
###end title 74
###begin p 75
###xml 134 137 134 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 212 216 212 216 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 281 285 281 285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR33">2001</xref>
###xml 301 305 301 305 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR31">2003</xref>
###xml 394 397 394 397 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 526 529 526 529 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
Analyses of the pheno-critical periods during development for eye induction implicate that there are two different signals initiating toy transcription: one occurring during the blastoderm stage (Kronhamn et al. 2002) and the other during the second larval instar (Kumar and Moses 2001; Kenyon et al. 2003). Our aim was to study the expression patterns of the 5-kb cis-regulatory region of the toy gene. In addition, we analyzed this sequence for presumptive protein-binding sites in order to understand how the expression of toy is regulated.
###end p 75
###begin p 76
###xml 52 55 52 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 227 230 227 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 348 351 348 351 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 402 405 402 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 432 436 432 436 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 465 469 465 469 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 528 532 528 532 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR41">1993</xref>
###xml 549 553 549 553 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR15">1994</xref>
###xml 567 571 567 571 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2003</xref>
###xml 604 608 604 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 700 707 700 707 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 738 741 738 741 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 746 748 746 748 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 789 792 789 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 864 871 864 871 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 968 971 968 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 971 974 971 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 971 974 971 974 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 983 988 983 988 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hsp70</italic>
###xml 1014 1019 1014 1019 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">pUAST</italic>
###xml 1065 1072 1065 1072 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 1239 1242 1239 1242 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1301 1304 1301 1304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 1451 1458 1451 1458 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 1601 1609 1601 1609 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy-Gal4</italic>
###xml 1652 1659 1652 1659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-P35</italic>
###xml 479 484 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 489 494 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
We conclude that the four constructs, including the toy promoter and 1,293 bp of surrounding DNA gave the expected expression pattern during embryonic as well as larval development. The putative Pax6-binding sites flanking the toy transcription start site might be of importance for initiation or maintenance of a correct expression pattern of the toy gene. Misexpression of Ey protein does not induce toy expression (Czerny et al. 1999). However, it is known that Pax6 genes in human and mouse are auto-regulated (Plaza et al. 1993; Epstein et al. 1994; Aota et al. 2003) in order to keep the activated Pax6 gene continuously expressed also when the initiating signal is not longer present. How can UAS-toy be capable of rescuing lethal toy and ey mutants without a driver construct when toy expression seems to be so tightly regulated? Our results show that the UAS-toy transgene is leaky. Either very little Toy protein is required to rescue the pupal lethality of toyhdl and the hsp70 promoter included in the pUAST vector is sufficient to support this, or the UAS-toy transgene carries cryptic enhancers or auto-regulatory sequences. We hypothesize that Toy protein can bind to, e.g., the two putative Pax6-binding sites found in the toy transcription unit and thus maintain transcription of the toy gene. In the absence of Toy, Ey protein can bind to these sites and induce a low level of transcription. This may be sufficient for up-regulating UAS-toy transgene expression to rescuing levels, causing the observed leakiness of the transgenic lines. This hypothesis is supported by the fact the toy-Gal4 driver is necessary to obtain rescue with UAS-P35.
###end p 76
###begin p 77
###xml 26 32 26 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 57 61 57 61 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR19">1995</xref>
###xml 135 139 135 139 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Gal4</italic>
###xml 228 230 228 230 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 230 231 230 231 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 230 231 230 231 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 252 258 252 258 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-ey</italic>
###xml 263 270 263 270 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 322 324 322 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 324 325 324 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 324 325 324 325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 439 442 439 442 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 446 448 446 448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 610 612 610 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 612 613 612 613 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 612 613 612 613 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
Analyses of the published UAS-ey sequence (Halder et al. 1995) show that it does not contain any putative Pax6-binding sites. Still, a Gal4 driver is not necessary to increase survival or improve the eye phenotype of homozygous eyD adults; one copy of UAS-ey (or UAS-toy) is sufficient. This could be due to the fact that eyD is not a null allele, and the truncated protein can resume some functions. An increased copy number of wild-type toy or ey genes is then sufficient to ameliorate head development. The phenotypic improvement should, however, not be expected to be better than that seen in heterozygous eyD individuals, which is in agreement with our observations.
###end p 77
###begin p 78
###xml 4 19 4 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D. melanogaster</italic>
###xml 19 21 19 21 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 42 46 42 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 147 151 147 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR48">1998</xref>
###xml 166 170 166 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR21">1999</xref>
###xml 189 193 189 193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR29">1999</xref>
###xml 209 213 209 213 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR1">2003</xref>
###xml 248 251 248 251 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 354 357 354 357 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
The D. melanogasterey gene and vertebrate Pax6 genes have been shown to have binding sites for regulatory proteins within introns (Williams et al. 1998; Hauck et al. 1999; Kammandel et al. 1999; Adachi et al. 2003). Further analyses of presumptive toy enhancer regions are underway, especially focusing on the introns, to elucidate what signals initiate toy transcription in the eye-antennal primordia.
###end p 78
###begin title 79
###xml 0 3 0 3 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
toy mutant phenotypes and cell death in eye discs
###end title 79
###begin p 80
###xml 5 9 5 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 22 32 22 32 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 223 226 223 226 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 231 233 231 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 247 257 247 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 479 482 479 482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 482 485 482 485 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 482 485 482 485 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 533 537 533 537 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
Both Pax6 paralogs in Drosophila are necessary for correct development and survival. Furthermore, it is evident from their differential expression in brain and VNC that there has been a subdivision of functions between the toy and ey genes during Drosophila evolution. However, a plethora of evidence has accumulated implying that their functions in the eye development pathway are overlapping and redundant. To corroborate these results we further analyzed the phenotype of the toyhdl mutant and investigated to what degree the two Pax6 transgenes could rescue these phenotypes.
###end p 80
###begin p 81
###xml 73 76 73 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 76 79 76 79 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 76 79 76 79 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 184 187 184 187 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 187 190 187 190 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 187 190 187 190 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 235 237 235 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 237 238 237 238 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 237 238 237 238 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 342 344 342 344 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 344 345 344 345 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 344 345 344 345 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 368 372 368 372 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">1998</xref>
###xml 504 508 504 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR33">2001</xref>
###xml 588 591 588 591 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">act</sup>
###xml 629 631 629 631 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 636 639 636 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 693 696 693 696 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 712 716 712 716 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR34">2000</xref>
###xml 773 775 773 775 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 842 846 842 846 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR31">2003</xref>
###xml 865 869 865 869 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR13">2004</xref>
###xml 968 971 968 971 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 971 974 971 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 971 974 971 974 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 1033 1037 1033 1037 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 1112 1115 1112 1115 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
Acridine orange staining shows a massive cell death in antennal discs of toyhdl homozyogous mutant larvae and we also observe that antennal discs are missing in a large portion of the toyhdl mutant larvae at third instar. In contrast, eyD mutant larvae mainly exhibit cell death in the eye disc, a phenotype very similar to that found in the ey2 mutant (Halder et al. 1998). In larvae, there are indications that the adult eye development is regulated by the Notch (N) signaling pathway (Kumar and Moses 2001). It is possible to induce ectopic eyes with the constitutively activated UAS-Nact. This induces the expression of both ey and toy in the growing eye, indicating that N is upstream of toy (Kurata et al. 2000). Other studies, however, argue that N does not control ey expression or eye identity, but instead eye growth (Kenyon et al. 2003; Dominguez et al. 2004). We have previously shown that the pheno-critical period for producing the headless phenotype in toyhdl mutants is during embryonic stages 12-16 (Kronhamn et al. 2002). It is, therefore, conceivable that the defects in eye-antennal discs of toy mutants are initiated when the small set of cells are allocated to form the eye-antennal primordium during gastrulation. If Toy is lacking, too few cells are set aside and this initial deficiency could be aggravated by apoptosis or a lower level of cell proliferation at later stages.
###end p 81
###begin p 82
###xml 31 34 31 34 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 34 37 34 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 34 37 34 37 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 250 251 250 251 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 503 506 503 506 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 506 509 506 509 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 506 509 506 509 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 914 918 914 918 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
The weakest adult phenotype of toyhdl mutants show lack of ocelli and cuticle derived from the ocellar part of the eye disc. A somewhat stronger phenotype is the "cleft head" where pharate adults lack substantial part of the dorsal medial head (Fig. 4f). These flies still retain the tissue derived from the antennal disc. An even stronger phenotype, "eye-on-thorax", is lacking antennal disc tissues, but still have compound eyes, which are positioned directly on the thorax. We sometimes observe that toyhdl homozygous headless pharate adults have masses of red pigment inside the thorax (not shown). This indicates that compound eyes can be formed, but that they are unable to evaginate during metamorphosis, probably because head cuticle, on which the eyes should sit, is not formed. The strongest phenotype (headless) is pharate adults lacking all domains derived from the eye-antennal discs (Kronhamn et al. 2002).
###end p 82
###begin p 83
###xml 69 72 69 72 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 115 117 115 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 117 118 117 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 117 118 117 118 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 123 125 123 125 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 125 126 125 126 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 125 126 125 126 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 270 274 270 274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">1998</xref>
###xml 291 293 291 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 293 294 293 294 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 293 294 293 294 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 322 324 322 324 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">so</italic>
###xml 324 325 324 325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</italic>
###xml 324 325 324 325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>1</italic></sup>
###xml 330 333 330 333 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">eya</italic>
###xml 333 334 333 334 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</italic>
###xml 333 334 333 334 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>1</italic></sup>
###xml 350 354 350 354 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR3">1993</xref>
###xml 372 376 372 376 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR9">1994</xref>
###xml 472 474 472 474 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 479 482 479 482 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 592 596 592 596 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">1999</xref>
###xml 642 646 642 646 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 800 804 800 804 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR44">2004</xref>
###xml 813 815 813 815 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 887 890 887 890 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
The deformation and cell death observed in the eye-antennal discs of toy mutants is clearly different from that in eyD and ey2 mutants, where the eye part is strongly reduced in size and subject to massive cell death, while the antennal portion is normal (Halder et al. 1998). Cell death in ey2 is very similar to that of so1 and eya1 (Bonini et al. 1993; Cheyette et al. 1994), two other genes specifying compound eyes. This shows that even if the expression patterns of ey and toy in early embryonic eye primordia and late larval eye-antennal imaginal discs are very similar (Czerny et al. 1999), the outcome of weaker mutations of the two Pax6 genes shows complementary phenotypes and is a good example of sub-functionality, which has also been pointed out by Gehring and co-workers (Punzo et al. 2004). While ey is vital for the development and differentiation of the compound eyes, toy is mainly needed for the development of the medial anterior, and dorsal parts of the head including antennae and ocelli.
###end p 83
###begin title 84
###xml 10 12 10 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
Rescue of ey mutants
###end title 84
###begin p 85
###xml 17 20 17 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 66 68 66 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 68 69 68 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</italic>
###xml 68 69 68 69 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>2</italic></sup>
###xml 87 89 87 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 89 94 89 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 89 94 89 94 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 127 131 127 131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR44">2004</xref>
###xml 158 160 158 160 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 160 165 160 165 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">J5.71</italic>
###xml 160 165 160 165 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>J5.71</italic></sup>
###xml 230 233 230 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 286 288 286 288 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 446 450 446 450 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR44">2004</xref>
###xml 459 460 459 460 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</sup>
###xml 607 611 607 611 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 635 637 635 637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 637 638 637 638 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 637 638 637 638 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 723 724 723 724 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</sup>
###xml 849 851 849 851 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">so</italic>
###xml 1061 1063 1061 1063 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1063 1064 1063 1064 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1063 1064 1063 1064 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 1095 1097 1095 1097 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1097 1098 1097 1098 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1097 1098 1097 1098 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 1290 1294 1290 1294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 1358 1362 1358 1362 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 1420 1421 1420 1421 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</sup>
###xml 1537 1539 1537 1539 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">so</italic>
###xml 1634 1636 1634 1636 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1636 1637 1636 1637 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 1636 1637 1636 1637 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
Misexpression of toy leads to the induction of ectopic eyes in an ey2 as well as in an eyJ5.71 mutant background (Punzo et al. 2004). We show that homozygous eyJ5.71 loss of function mutant flies can be fully rescued by increased toy transcription, without any accompanying increase in ey expression. Thus, we conclude that Toy can promote eye and head development in an Ey-independent manner, which has also been suggested earlier (Punzo et al. 2004). The EyD protein not only lacks the entire homeodomain, but also 660 amino acids in the C-terminus, giving the dominant eyeless phenotype (Kronhamn et al. 2002). The dominance of the eyD allele is due to either a gain-of-function or a dominant-negative function of the EyD protein. The remaining paired domain might still be able to bind to the cluster of binding sites within the eye enhancer of so, but the modifications in the C-terminus might interfere with normal transcriptional activation. We show that over-expression of either Ey or Toy proteins, respectively, can rescue the lethality of homozygous eyD mutants and also suppress the eyD phenotype and partially restore head development, and we have previously shown that the lethality could also be rescued by targeted expression of the apoptosis inhibitor P35 (Kronhamn et al. 2002). This seems to contradict a division of functions between the Pax6 paralogs in development, but a possibility is that the EyD protein (due to its conformational changes) cannot discriminate between Ey- and Toy-binding sites (for instance in so) and thus interferes with both developmental pathways. Such a scenario could also explain why eyD homozygous flies obtain a headless phenotype, whereas loss-of-function mutants do not.
###end p 85
###begin title 86
Rescue from pupal lethality is caused by increased head size
###end title 86
###begin p 87
###xml 44 47 44 47 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 47 50 47 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 47 50 47 50 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 52 55 52 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 55 59 55 59 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">G739</italic>
###xml 55 59 55 59 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>G739</italic></sup>
###xml 59 60 59 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">,</italic>
###xml 65 67 65 67 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 67 68 67 68 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 67 68 67 68 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>D</italic></sup>
###xml 411 415 411 415 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR37">1970</xref>
###xml 484 487 484 487 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 487 490 487 490 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 487 490 487 490 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 750 753 750 753 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS</italic>
The major lethal phase of headless mutants, toyhdl, toyG739, and eyD, is the pharate adult stage, when flies are ready to escape from the pupal case. One very important head structure for this process is the ptilinum, an extensible sac which is blown up by the pharate adult under hydrostatic pressure to break open the pupal lid. This structure is formed by the hinge region in the eye-antennal disc (Ouweneel 1970). This particular portion shows evidence of extensive cell death in toyhdl mutants. A somewhat smaller head or an undeveloped ptilinum may make it impossible to break out from the pupa. We were able to partially rescue the three headless mutants from the pupal lethality by expressing Toy protein or Ey protein in eye primordia using UAS constructs. Also with the caspase inhibitor P35, we increased survival with similar efficiencies. This indicates that exogenous Pax6 proteins may have anti-apoptotic effects. Alternatively, ectopic expression of Toy or Ey induces proliferation and increases the number of cells set aside in the eye-antennal primordium during gastrulation resulting in an increased head size, which allows pharates to escape from pupal cases. A similar result could be achieved by P35-induced inhibition of apoptosis during later stages.
###end p 87
###begin title 88
###xml 22 26 22 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
Dosage sensitivity of Pax6
###end title 88
###begin p 89
###xml 7 10 7 10 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 10 13 10 13 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 10 13 10 13 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 132 136 132 136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR32">2002</xref>
###xml 602 605 602 605 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 605 608 605 608 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 605 608 605 608 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 729 732 711 714 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 761 764 743 746 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 764 767 746 749 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">hdl</italic>
###xml 764 767 746 749 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><italic>hdl</italic></sup>
###xml 787 794 769 776 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">UAS-toy</italic>
###xml 846 850 828 832 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Gal4</italic>
###xml 1208 1212 1190 1194 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR11">2000</xref>
###xml 1248 1252 1230 1234 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR28">2001</xref>
In the toyhdl mutant stock we observe an extreme temperature-dependent variability in the phenotypic manifestation (Kronhamn et al. 2002). One explanation for this could be a low affinity of wild-type Ey protein for Toy binding sites. At lower temperatures, the slow development allows Ey to bind in sufficient amounts to inhibit apoptosis and promote the developmental pathway. However, at higher temperatures, when development is rapid, not enough activation of target genes takes place, causing fewer founder cells and subsequent lethality. Interestingly, we find that it is only possible to rescue toyhdl mutants from lethality when cultures are kept at lower temperatures (15degrees to 22degrees). At 25degrees we find that toy mRNA levels are elevated in toyhdl flies carrying the UAS-toy construct and that this increase is independent of Gal4 driver constructs. Since the rescue at higher temperatures is very poor, we conclude that this increase in Toy expression levels results in lethality. Other publications also suggest that surplus of Pax6 protein function is detrimental to eye development. Over-expression of Ey protein in the eye discs leads to a reduced eye phenotype (Curtiss and Mlodzik 2000). Noll and co-workers (Jiao et al. 2001) have shown that over-expression of Pax proteins in the eye primordia results in interference of the developmental pathway and headless phenotypes. They also showed that this interference can only be induced during the first half of the embryonic development, when the eye-antennal primordium is formed and that the interference of the developmental pathway could be inhibited by ectopic expression of cell proliferation factors.
###end p 89
###begin p 90
###xml 15 19 15 19 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 78 82 78 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 157 161 157 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">1992</xref>
###xml 248 252 248 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 265 269 265 269 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR47">1991</xref>
###xml 283 286 283 286 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Sey</italic>
###xml 380 384 380 384 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR24">1986</xref>
###xml 443 447 443 447 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 632 636 632 636 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR18">1994</xref>
###xml 655 659 655 659 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 684 694 684 694 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 784 786 784 786 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 840 843 840 843 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 888 898 888 898 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 898 902 898 902 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 910 913 910 913 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">toy</italic>
###xml 918 920 918 920 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">ey</italic>
###xml 1055 1059 1055 1059 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Pax6</italic>
###xml 139 143 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 171 176 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">human</span>
###xml 287 291 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mice</span>
###xml 461 467 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">humans</span>
The vertebrate Pax6 homolog is involved in development of the vertebrate eye. Pax6 null alleles give a small-eye phenotype in heterozygous mice (Hill et al. 1992) and the human eye defect anririda (loss of iris) results from haplo-insufficiency of Pax6 (Ton et al. 1991). Homozygous Sey mice die at birth, lacking eyes and nose, and having severely malformed brains (Hogan et al. 1986). Similarly, rare incidents of compound heterozygotes for Pax6 mutations in humans result in lethality; including lack of eyes, a malformed nasal region, and severe brain defects, where the cerebral hemispheres are widely separated (Glaser et al. 1994). This shows that Pax6 in vertebrates, like in Drosophila, is extremely dosage-sensitive and that heterozygous mutants show a phenotype similar to ey mutants, while the homozygous phenotype resemble the toy mutant phenotype. Thus, it seems as the two DrosophilaPax6 genes, toy and ey, have acquired a certain degree of subfunctionality during evolution, and the two copies together reflect the functions of the single Pax6 gene in vertebrates.
###end p 90
